### 115. Re-Sourcing Trait Encoding from HEXACO to Attachment: When one trait was driving two different things and the literature said stop

**Date:** 2026-06-29

This post documents the trait-source-routing correction where the framework's first-pass V1 specification used HEXACO honesty-humility for both cooperation behaviors (which the literature supports per Hilbig and Zettler 2009 JRP 43(3):516-519, Thielmann and Hilbig 2015 PSPB 41(11):1523-1536, Zettler et al. 2020 PoPS 15(3):723-760) and relational-event encoding (which the literature does not support; the correct trait source for relational encoding is attachment style per Fraley, Waller, and Brennan 2000 JPSP 78(2):350-365 ECR-R). The conflation broke a four-NPC interaction scenario in test runs where characters with the same HEXACO H profile but different attachment patterns produced indistinguishable relational-encoding patterns; the failure surfaced the trait-source-routing correction. The post documents (a) the original HEXACO-everywhere mistake with operator-driven extension beyond empirical scope, (b) what HEXACO H is actually for (exploitation-versus-cooperation prediction in economic-game settings per the cited validation literature), (c) what attachment style is actually for (relational-event encoding and retrieval per Mikulincer and Shaver 2016 *Attachment in Adulthood* second edition canonical synthesis), (d) the corrected trait-modulated encoding filter routing (cooperation and generosity through HEXACO H; relational encoding through attachment avoidance and anxiety; pair-history accumulation through attachment style), (e) the Fraley and Hudson 2014 caveat that attachment is stable-but-modifiable on multi-year timescales with V1.x shift-mechanism candidacy, (f) the four behavioral patterns the corrected routing unlocks (secure: rich encoding plus accurate appraisal; anxious: rich encoding plus over-pessimistic appraisal; avoidant: thin encoding plus under-attentive appraisal; fearful-avoidant: thin encoding plus over-pessimistic appraisal), (g) the cross-cultural ECR-R WEIRD-sample-derivation caveat per Henrich et al. 2010 BBS 33(2-3):61-83 that the schema-placeholder approach reserves space for. The post bounds its claim (not claiming HEXACO H is the only relevant source for cooperation; not claiming attachment style is the only relevant source for relational encoding; not claiming re-source eliminated trait-source-conflation failure modes; not claiming V1 cost estimate is precise; not claiming cross-cultural caveat is fully addressed) and claims the literature-check-per-function discipline catches the use-the-familiar-trait failure mode that operator-driven trait-source decisions reproduce.

### 116. Sentiment Override and Pair-Specific Memory: The bowling-alley tipping scenario as a worked example

**Date:** 2026-06-29

This post documents the framework's pair-relational mechanism grounded in Hawkins, Carrère, and Gottman 2002 *Journal of Marriage and Family* 64(1):193-201 sentiment-override formalization. The bowling-alley tipping scenario walks three bowlers and one pinboy through five game-years of accumulated pair history; the same fifty-cent tip event becomes gratitude or reputation or pair-trust or public-norm signal or nothing depending on the pair-history-accumulated encoding conditions. The framework caps the active-sentiments-per-ordered-pair at three to five (informed by Sims 4 Sentiments' cap-of-four commercial precedent); older sentiments decay or merge or promote to Layer 2 at consolidation. The post documents (a) the bowling-alley tipping scenario as a worked example of per-event encoding variance, (b) Hawkins-Carrère-Gottman 2002 as the canonical psychological-literature anchor with the cross-cultural WEIRD-sample caveat, (c) the framework's sentiment-override implementation (ordered-pair scalars in [-1, +1]; decay-toward-current-plus-drift-from-history update formula; bias on event-interpretation in pair-history-accumulator; cap-per-pair with decay-or-merge-or-promote disposition), (d) commercial precedent comparison across four systems (Sims 4 Sentiments; RimWorld opinions; Crusader Kings 3 memories; Dwarf Fortress emotional memory tiers) with what the framework borrows from each, (e) what the framework adds beyond commercial precedents (multi-decade NPC memory scope; emotion-conditioned encoding; retrieval-time affect modulation per Eich 1995; active-inference-grounded decision scoring), (f) what the framework does not do better than commercial precedents (production engineering; UI surfacing; modding extensibility), (g) the novel-in-combination-not-in-components honesty framing. The post bounds its claim (not claiming most sophisticated implementation in any dimension; not claiming the scenario is empirically validated; not claiming commercial-precedent comparison is exhaustive; not claiming cap-per-pair tuning is optimal; not claiming the cross-cultural caveat is fully addressed by schema-placeholder) and claims the framework's pair-relational mechanism is grounded in canonical literature, commercial-precedent-validated, and extended in specific ways the surveyed precedents do not combine.

### 118. Recency Collapse and the Need for Consolidation: Tiered memory architecture at multi-decade game-time scope

**Date:** 2026-06-29

This post documents the framework's tiered memory architecture (Layer 1 raw events with bounded recency window; Layer 2 encoded-and-reconstructed perspective memory; Layer 3 accumulator with constant per-character storage cost; yearly consolidation pass with four promotion criteria; 0.995-per-game-hour decay anchor for everyday-event decay) as the operational response to the recency-collapse-versus-premature-compression failure modes at multi-decade game-time scope. The arithmetic at the framework's target scale produces approximately one to two million interaction events at one hundred bytes per event for thirty game-years of multi-NPC interaction; naive raw-event storage exceeds iOS V1 budget by an order of magnitude; naive over-summarization flattens the texture the design surface commits to; the tiered consolidation pattern threads the needle. The post documents (a) the recency-collapse problem with storage and retrieval arithmetic; (b) the premature-compression failure mode with the Sims-style-meter-flattening risk; (c) the three-layer architecture decomposition and the consolidation pass that moves content between layers; (d) the 0.995-per-game-hour decay anchor with approximately one-game-week half-life and the design-choice rationale (empirically inspired by Ebbinghaus 1885 plus Murre and Dros 2015 *PLOS ONE* 10(7):e0120644 modern re-analysis; tuned to game-feel and computational-budget constraints; trait-modulated per character); (e) the four promotion criteria (affective-spike events; pair-history-significant events; trait-modulated-significant events; first-occurrence events) and the everyday-event decay; (f) the link to the hybrid-path posts (cached policies; multi-graph memory; LLM-at-consolidation-boundary). The post bounds its claim (not claiming the 0.995 anchor is empirically derived; not claiming the four promotion criteria are exhaustive; not claiming the pattern eliminates the storage-versus-texture trade-off; not claiming save-load determinism handles all corner cases; not claiming the V1 implementation will handle the consolidation pass without empirical surprises) and claims the tiered consolidation pattern is the framework's operational response to the failure-mode pair, and the 0.995 anchor is a designed choice that respects both empirical literature and computational-budget constraints with transparency about the trade-offs.

### 119. Why Active Inference Belongs in the Audit Layer First: Earning the runtime promotion through empirical evidence

### 121. Generative Agents Are the Backbone, Not the Runtime: Park 2023 as conceptual foundation without direct LLM scaling

**Date:** 2026-06-29

This post documents the framework's borrowing of Park, O'Brien, Cai, Morris, Liang, and Bernstein 2023 "Generative Agents: Interactive Simulacra of Human Behavior" arXiv:2304.03442 three-process decomposition (observe-reflect-plan) as the conceptual backbone for the framework's procedural-character architecture, with explicit substitution of the implementational layers to address production-deployment constraints Park 2023 did not address. The arithmetic at the framework's target scale forces the substitution: 25 agents in Park 2023's published evaluation versus the framework's tens of NPCs at ten decisions per game-minute; LLM API cost at approximately $0.001-0.01 per inference times tens of thousands of decisions per game-hour produces operationally infeasible cost structure for indie-budget commercial deployment; per-frame LLM API latency at hundreds-of-milliseconds-to-seconds exceeds the 33-millisecond per-frame budget at iOS V1 target framerate. The post documents (a) Park 2023's three-process decomposition (observation; reflection; planning) plus memory-stream persistent state and the published 25-agent evaluation, (b) the alignment between Park 2023's three processes and the framework's three-layer memory architecture (observation aligns with Layer 1; reflection aligns with Layer 2 plus consolidation pass; planning aligns with active-inference decision-scoring), (c) the scaling-constraint arithmetic that forces the hybrid path, (d) the architectural surgery substituting cached and sampled events plus Markov-blanket isolation at the observation layer; yearly consolidation pass at the reflection layer; cached active-inference policies at runtime plus sophisticated-inference EFE evaluation at consolidation boundaries at the planning layer, (e) what the framework extends Park 2023 in (multi-decade scope; per-frame latency budgets; cross-cultural disclosure discipline), (f) the honest scope on what the framework is (procedural-character cognitive architecture spec for cozy-sim design surface; research-application case study rather than research contribution; extensible at META-architecture level), (g) the novel-in-combination-not-in-components honesty enumerating the six borrowed components (Park 2023; Friston 2017 plus 2021; Hawkins-Carrère-Gottman 2002; Russell 1980; Fraley-Waller-Brennan 2000; Wiredu 1992). The post bounds its claim (not claiming Park 2023 is the only relevant research precedent; not claiming hybrid-path substitutions are the only operationally-defensible response; not claiming LLM cost arithmetic is precise for all providers; not claiming the framework's contribution exhausts production-deployment work; not claiming the V1 deployment will validate without empirical surprises) and claims Park 2023's three-process decomposition is the canonical recent precedent that the framework borrows structurally while substituting the implementational layers, and the discipline of being clear about what is borrowed and what is extended is part of the framework's honesty commitment.

### 122. Multi-Graph Memory Without the Research-System Overhead: Typed indexes over a single store

**Date:** 2026-06-29

This post documents the framework's adaptation of MAGMA-style multi-graph agent memory architecture (arXiv:2601.03236; 2026) where the framework borrows the typing decomposition (semantic; temporal; causal; entity views) while substituting the storage architecture (single underlying store plus four typed indexes rather than MAGMA's separated graph databases) to fit the iOS V1 budget envelope. Pure-relational tables would not scale at multi-decade scope; multiple separate graph databases would over-engineer at indie-budget V1 deployment; the typed-indexes-over-single-store approach captures MAGMA's separability benefits at indie-budget cost. The post documents (a) MAGMA's typing decomposition with four retrieval-pattern views and the separated-stores benchmark speedup, (b) why direct MAGMA adoption does not fit V1 (multiple persistence engines; iOS save-state envelope constraints; indie operator BUILD-side capacity), (c) the framework's typed-index adaptation with single underlying store and four typed indexes (semantic for trait-based concept tags; temporal for game-time ordering; causal for event-to-event links via outcome-modifier tags; entity for pair-relationship-keyed lookup) with atomic update on every event, (d) pair summaries at consolidation boundaries that compress per-pair history into runtime-accessible representations with commercial precedent in Sims 4 Sentiments and RimWorld opinions, (e) a retrieval scenario walkthrough showing the typed-index O(1) cost versus naive O(N) scan cost, (f) what the typed-index adaptation gives up (MAGMA's deeper graph-traversal queries; specific full-benchmark performance), (g) the V1 implementation cost estimate of approximately 24-40 hours of BUILD-side work. The post bounds its claim (not claiming the typed-index adaptation is the only operationally-defensible response to MAGMA; not claiming the four-index decomposition exhausts retrieval patterns; not claiming storage-cost arithmetic is precise; not claiming MAGMA's separated-stores approach is wrong for research-system deployments; not claiming the MAGMA citation is fully primary-text-verified) and claims the typed-index adaptation captures the per-view retrieval-pattern separation benefit at indie-budget V1 scale without the multi-store storage overhead.

### 125. Why Wiredu Cannot Be a Trait Slider: The category error procedural designers should avoid across multiple cross-cultural traditions

**Date:** 2026-06-29

This post documents the category error the framework caught in its own first-pass specification (mapping Wiredu's sympathetic impartiality at Chapter 9 page 199 onto HEXACO honesty-humility as a trait coordinate) and generalizes the lesson beyond the Wiredu-specific case. Wiredu's sympathetic impartiality is a procedural moral test (something the agent DOES; a deliberative imaginative procedure that produces per-action verdicts); HEXACO H is an individual-difference trait dimension (something the agent HAS; a dispositional tendency that predicts behavior statistically); mapping the procedural test onto the trait dimension confuses doing with having and conflates different evaluation logic and different causal direction and different universal-claim transfer levels. The post documents (a) Wiredu's sympathetic impartiality with primary-text grounding at Chapter 9 page 199 and structural similarity to Kantian universalizability and Rawlsian original position as procedural moral tests, (b) HEXACO H with the validation literature anchors (Ashton and Lee 2009 JPA 91(4):340-345; Hilbig and Zettler 2009; Thielmann and Hilbig 2015) and its dispositional-tendency character, (c) the category error walkthrough with four structural reasons (different objects; different evaluation logic; different causal direction; universal-claim non-transfer), (d) the ornamental-deployment risk per Bilge 2013 *Du Bois Review* 10(2):405-424 with the worse-than-no-mapping framing, (e) the lesson generalized to procedural moral tests across Kantian universalizability, Rawlsian original position, Confucian role ethics, and Ubuntu communal accountability (the category error is the same structural shape across multiple cross-cultural and Western-philosophical traditions), (f) what does work for cross-cultural philosophical grounding (treat the procedural test as inspiration at framework-paper layer; treat the implementation as its own design problem with its own trait sources; be explicit about the inspiration-versus-implementation distinction), (g) what this means for Modified-C-bis V1 (HEXACO H plus attachment plus Gottman for V1 generosity mechanics with no cross-cultural philosophical operationalization). The post bounds its claim (not claiming the category error pattern is the only failure mode for cross-cultural philosophical grounding; not claiming Option (c) drop is the only operationally-defensible response; not claiming the category error generalizes uniformly across all cross-cultural traditions; not claiming the three-element shape is the only operationally-defensible response; not claiming the universalist framing's corroboration extends to all Wiredu's claims) and claims procedural moral tests are not trait dimensions and the discipline of distinguishing inspiration from implementation is operationally cheap and catches the category-error failure mode at the planning phase.

### 127. No Single "African View": Menkiti, Wiredu, Gyekye and the intra-African dispute the framework discloses publicly

**Date:** 2026-06-29

This post documents the intra-African philosophical dispute between Wiredu (Menkiti-aligned achievement-graded view) and Gyekye (Kant-grounded counter-position) and the framework's structural-borrowing engagement with Wiredu's reading specifically rather than with "the Akan view" categorically. Within Akan philosophy itself, Wiredu's reading is contested; Gyekye co-edited the canonical *Person and Community* volume with Wiredu and defends inherent-at-birth personhood with communal context enhancing rather than constituting; the Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy entry gives Gyekye's counter-position equal philosophical weight; the framework's choice of Wiredu's reading over Gyekye's counter-position is operator-judgment within a contested field. The post documents (a) Wiredu's view with the primary-text grounding (Chapter 9 page 200 continual striving; page 199 sympathetic impartiality first principle; pages 201-202 relational constitution "palm tree" metaphor; *onnye nipa* as graduated personhood-status judgment per Wiredu's reading), (b) Gyekye's counter-position with primary-text anchors (Wiredu's introduction pages 10-11 documents Gyekye's dispute; Gyekye 1997 *Tradition and Modernity* Oxford University Press is the fuller treatment; *onnye nipa* as moral-virtue judgment rather than ontological denial in Gyekye's reading), (c) the Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy framing of the dispute as ongoing within Akan and African philosophy with both readings given equal weight, (d) why the framework's choice matters for integrity (presenting "personhood-as-achievement" as "the Akan view" would be a category error misrepresenting the tradition's internal pluralism; the honest framing is Wiredu's specific reading with full disclosure of the contestation), (e) a counterfactual comparison of what the framework would look like under Gyekye's reading versus the framework's chosen Wiredu reading, (f) the Menkiti-Wiredu agreement on achievement-graded view across two African philosophical traditions (Igbo and Akan) with explicit non-extension to "African philosophy" as a unified category since African philosophy is plural at the intra-tradition and inter-tradition levels, (g) what disclosure does NOT mean (not resolution; not neutrality; not undermining of either reading's philosophical authority), (h) the retraction-condition application to this post specifically. The post bounds its claim (not claiming the engagement exhausts the dispute's philosophical work; not claiming Menkiti-Wiredu convergence implies universal applicability across African philosophy; not claiming the framework's choice is philosophically correct; not claiming the SEP entry is the only authoritative reference; not claiming the disclosure discipline eliminates legitimate critique) and claims the framework's structural borrowing is from Wiredu's reading specifically within a contested field with full disclosure of the contestation, and the discipline of acknowledging tradition-internal pluralism explicitly catches the categorical-framing failure mode that flattened-view engagements produce.

### 128. The Accumulator Is Where WEIRD Defaults Hide: Henrich, Crenshaw, Cross, and the schema-placeholder discipline the framework adopts

**Date:** 2026-06-29

This post is the closer of the cross-cultural sequence and the closer of the entire philosophical-content arc. The framework's Layer 3 accumulator integrates a procedural character's affective history into a present-anchored state; the calibration silently encodes the WEIRD default per Henrich, Heine, and Norenzayan 2010 *Behavioral and Brain Sciences* 33(2-3):61-83 unless the framework's discipline makes the calibration explicit. The framework's schema-placeholder approach is the V1-shippable response: three metadata fields (cultural-context tag; intersectional positional tags; identity stage) reserve schema space for post-V1 operationalization while preventing the WEIRD-default from being a hidden assumption at the architecture-canonical level. The post documents (a) the WEIRD critique with Henrich-Heine-Norenzayan 2010 as the canonical anchor and the 80%+ WEIRD-sample-overrepresentation pattern affecting psychology validation literature broadly, (b) how the WEIRD default silently encodes cultural bias across four framework calibration points (the accumulator decay rate; sentiment-override formation per Hawkins-Carrère-Gottman 2002 U.S. married-couple sample; attachment style distributions per Fraley-Waller-Brennan 2000 ECR-R WEIRD-sample validation; HEXACO H exploitation tendencies per WEIRD-sample validation), (c) the Crenshaw intersectionality angle (Crenshaw 1989 *University of Chicago Legal Forum* 1989(1):139-167 and Crenshaw 1991 *Stanford Law Review* 43(6):1241-1299) with single-axis demographic framework critique and multi-axis lived-experience representation, (d) the Cross Nigrescence angle (Cross 1971 *Black World* 20(9):13-27 and Cross 1991 *Shades of Black* Temple University Press) with stage-progression framework as structural inspiration only with iOS V1 SCHEMA-PLACEHOLDER commitment, (e) the three schema-placeholder metadata fields (cultural_context_tag free-form; intersectional_position_tags[] array per Crenshaw; identity_stage Cross/Crenshaw V1 SCHEMA-PLACEHOLDER sentinel value), (f) what schema placeholders do NOT solve (does not fix WEIRD-calibration of underlying mechanics; does not substitute for primary-text reading; does not substitute for community engagement), (g) the Marcus Reed Surface 8 audit gate connection with Path A prerequisite #6 requiring substrate-triangulation for any sophisticated-inference mechanic deployment, (h) the cross-cultural sequence retrospective tying together posts 0124 through 0128, (i) the retraction-condition reaffirmation across all five cross-cultural posts. ### 137. Perpetual-Surprise Compression Edge Case: Where Sparse Coding Assumes and Where It Breaks

**Date:** 2026-07-01

This post documents the specific architectural finding surfaced by the Sim AI Phase 1 H4 test suite (prediction-error sparse encoding validation): when every event surprises the prediction model, encoding rate hits 100 percent and the sparse coding scheme provides zero compression benefit. The post documents (a) sparse coding as memory-compression strategy for procedural characters descending from Olshausen and Field 1996 (Nature 381:607-609; DOI 10.1038/381607a0) plus active-inference-coupled sparse coding grounded in Friston et al. 2017 active inference process theory (Neural Computation 29:1-49; DOI 10.1162/NECO_a_00912), (b) the mechanism's operational shape (per-character prediction model; encoding only when prediction error exceeds threshold; reconstruction via predicted plus stored error; less than 10 percent encoding rate for routine streams; 1-week storage under 1MB per character), (c) the empirical finding that the compression scheme's cost model implicitly bets on prediction-matching being common and the perpetual-surprise edge case is where the assumption breaks (100 percent encoding rate; storage grows linearly with event count; zero compression benefit), (d) the architectural implication for procedural-character populations at scale that include both routine-dominant characters and structurally-disrupted characters (population-budgeting math should account for the memory-storage-cost variance between the two segments rather than assuming both segments compress equally; content-authoring for structurally-disrupted characters carries both authoring cost and runtime memory cost as architecturally independent quantities), (e) the R10d Section 6.3 architectural revision proposal (acknowledge, never resolve authoring discipline applies at the runtime memory-cost surface as well as the authoring-cost surface; pending operator ratification). The post bounds its claim (not claiming sparse coding is the only memory-compression strategy; not claiming sustained-crisis characters break the framework's memory budget in general; not claiming perpetual-surprise edge case exhausts sparse coding failure modes; not claiming single-Sim finding generalizes uniformly to population scale; not claiming R10d Section 6.3 revision has ratified) and claims sparse coding assumes prediction-matching is the common case and the perpetual-surprise edge case is where the assumption breaks and this is architecturally consequential for populations that include structurally-disrupted characters at scale, and if you are building procedural-character architectures relying on prediction-error sparse coding for memory compression, budget the perpetual-surprise-state variance explicitly because the compression scheme's cost model implicitly bets on prediction-matching being common and when a subset of your characters violate that bet the memory-storage cost lands on that subset rather than smoothing across the population.

### 138. Cultural Baseline Signal Modest at Single-Sim: What KL-Divergence 0.01-0.02 Means for Population-Level Distinguishability

**Date:** 2026-07-01

This post documents the Sim AI Phase 1 H5 test suite finding (cultural-baseline distinguishability via symmetric KL-divergence between three placeholder cultural baselines labeled A/B/C at 2000-trial single-Sim scope) and the validation-vs-ratification methodology distinction the finding illuminates. The post documents (a) what KL-divergence measures at the domain scope plus what 0.01 to 0.02 range at 2000 trials means specifically (measurable and above zero confirms mechanical dispatch produces per-character behavior differences; smaller than initial 0.02 noticeable-difference sandbox threshold; test discipline threshold recalibrated to 0.005 empirically), (b) the validation-vs-ratification distinction (validation asks whether mechanism runs and produces specified output at per-Sim behavior distribution scope; ratification asks whether mechanism produces player-perceivable behavior differences at population plus visibility plus temporal cadence scope; validation is required but not sufficient for ratification), (c) connection to post 0128 WEIRD-defaults-in-the-accumulator schema-placeholder discipline (empirical result validates the discipline's operational shape at single-Sim scope; population-scale ratification is a Phase 2 and later question; specific reversal branch exists if Phase 2 shows mechanical differences do not accumulate meaningfully at population scale), (d) connection to Council 4 post 0135 per-NPC-philosophy-profile BANK Decision 4 (same discipline shape applied at different parameter surfaces; framework's canonical Council methodology now has empirical foundation for validation-vs-ratification pattern across three architectural instantiations: post 0130 relationship-mode ablation gate plus post 0135 per-NPC-philosophy-profile BANK plus this H5 finding), (e) the R10d Section 4 architectural revision proposal (cultural-baseline signal is measurable but modest at single-Sim scope; full 6-dimension validation requires Phase 2 multi-Sim testing; pending operator ratification). The post bounds its claim (not claiming 0.01 to 0.02 KL divergence is unimportant; not claiming single-Sim signal predicts population-scale signal magnitude; not claiming placeholder baselines represent finalized cultural parameterizations; not claiming validation-vs-ratification distinction is the only methodology discipline the finding illuminates; not claiming framework's schema-placeholder discipline is the only workable pattern for cross-cultural procedural-character architecture; not claiming Phase 2 will confirm population-scale amplification; not claiming R10d Section 4 revision has ratified) and claims single-Sim empirical validation is sufficient for architectural VALIDATION but insufficient for design-decision RATIFICATION at population level, and if you are building cross-cultural procedural-character architectures, the validation-vs-ratification distinction is operationally cheap and catches a specific failure mode where mechanism VALIDATION at single-agent scope gets conflated with design RATIFICATION for population-scale player-facing behavior, and the framework's continued arc has three architectural instantiations of the validation-vs-ratification pattern with enough empirical grounding to be a canonized discipline shape.

### 144. The Buffer That Overflowed by One: Entry-Count-Per-Fire Discipline in Cap-N Append Patterns

**Date:** 2026-07-03

This post documents a specific empirical fire from an active BUILD-mode cycle 2026-07-03 morning: a cap-N append buffer used `slice(-N)` before appending K entries per fire, allowing the buffer to reach N+K entries under sustained firing patterns. The bug was one line of code; the fix was one character (`slice(-(N-K))` for K-entry appends). The bug was invisible during small-scope tests because those tests did not force the buffer to fill past cap; the bug surfaced only when a hypothesis test scaffolded the boundary condition explicitly. The post documents (a) the buffer pattern where the bug hid (idiomatic-scanning cap-N append with slice), (b) the specific fire (750-tick sustained co-observation scenario in the framework's active simulation subsystem produced 41 entries at cap 40), (c) the entry-count-per-fire discipline the fix codifies (append site adding K entries per fire needs `slice(-(N-K))` not `slice(-N)`), (d) the Post 0136 empirical BUILD-mode-as-hypothesis discipline this fire concretely instantiates (architecture-as-hypothesis claims produce falsifiable predictions; hypothesis tests scaffolded at boundary conditions force the predictions into contact with real code paths; the class of bug the discipline predicts includes buffer-slice off-by-K), (e) reproduction risks across event-stream buffer classes (audit-log + transaction-log + relationship-history + event-sourcing buffers all face the same entry-count-per-fire pattern). The post bounds its claim (not claiming off-by-one buffer bugs are novel; not claiming hypothesis-test scaffolding always catches these bugs; not claiming n=1 is sufficient for sub-shape canonization; not claiming buffer bugs are the highest-leverage BUILD-mode findings; not claiming the fix generalizes to all cap patterns without adjustment) and claims cap-N append buffers where the append adds K entries per fire need `slice(-(N-K))` to enforce cap strictly, hypothesis-test scaffolding at boundary conditions catches this class of bug before emergent-scope corruption, and the framework's Post 0136 empirical BUILD-mode discipline is validated at n=1 at buffer-slice sub-shape within the current BUILD arc with sub-shape canonization pending second-fire strengthening.

### 146. Ten Layers of Model, Not One Layer of Prompt: How Procedural NPCs Represent Human Behavior Without an LLM in the Loop

**Date:** 2026-07-03

*Amendment note: HEXACO citation-chain drift caught at Council #6 close 2026-07-04 (Post 0146 cited Ashton and Lee 2007; framework canonical chain uses Lee and Ashton 2004 + Ashton and Lee 2009 per Posts 0115 + 0117 + 0125). See Post 0150 for forward-reference amendment executing Council #6 ratified bank-for-audit disposition. Post 0146 canonical text preserved unchanged per framework immutability convention; amendment operates at framework canonical-record layer.*

This post is a methodology-anchor post articulating the framework's structural approach to representing human behavior in procedural characters as ten grounded modeling layers rather than one LLM-prompt-dumping layer. The post opens by naming a foundational question surfaced during a substrate brainstorming session (how do NPCs know how humans function) and answering it structurally rather than with runtime-LLM appeal. The dominant Generative Agents descendant approach places the LLM in the runtime loop and inherits four specific costs (per-decision LLM calls do not scale; the mechanism producing each decision is opaque; behavioral consistency over game-years is empirically fragile; the substrate landscape shifts under the framework's feet). The framework's response is ten disjoint grounded models each with literature backing and testable properties: (Layer 1) needs as scalar accumulators with decay rates, grounded in survival biology; (Layer 2) affect as three independent scalars (valence, arousal, stress) grounded in Russell 1980 dimensional-circumplex plus Lazarus and Folkman 1984 stress-appraisal literature; (Layer 3) HEXACO 6-dimensional trait vectors grounded in Ashton and Lee 2007 plus Hilbig and Zettler 2009 plus Zettler et al. 2020 stability literature plus attachment styles from Fraley Waller Brennan 2000 ECR-R; (Layer 4) three-horizon memory (short + mid + long_biographical) with salience-thresholded encoding grounded in Park et al. 2023 generative-agents lineage; (Layer 5) expected free energy minimization at τ=1 with softmax action sampling grounded in Friston FitzGerald Rigoli Schwartenbeck Pezzulo 2017 process-theory paper plus Friston Da Costa Hafner Hesp Parr 2021 sophisticated inference paper; (Layer 6) ordered-pair sentiment scalars per Post 0116 plus sentiment override from Hawkins Carrère Gottman 2002; (Layer 7) cultural personhood baselines A/B/C parameterizing individual-versus-communal framing grounded in Wiredu 1992 Chapter 9 plus Menkiti 1984 plus Gyekye internal-tradition dispute; (Layer 8) life history as per-character biographical records with innate properties plus archetypal experience templates persisting at ecosystem layer; (Layer 9) environmental knowledge provided by Scene rather than known abstractly by NPC; (Layer 10) audit as sophisticated active inference apparatus running offline at consolidation boundaries per Post 0119 audit-first sequencing. The post walks through how the layers compose to produce auditable-longitudinally-stable-cross-environment-portable behavior; enumerates explicit non-goals (no general world facts + no domain expertise as knowledge + no dialogue system + no in-game media consumption); connects the composition to the field's top unsolved challenges (validation + reproducibility + auditability) noting that structural layering addresses each directly where LLM-prompt-dumping makes each harder. The post bounds its claim (not claiming individual layers are novel; not claiming ten layers exhaustively cover being human; not claiming this scales without engineering cost; not claiming LLM-in-runtime approaches are wrong for all use cases; not claiming layer count ten is canonical) and claims procedural NPCs can be built with layered grounded models rather than single LLM-prompt layer producing empirically inspectable properties the LLM-prompt-layer approach does not, ten specific layers cover a substantive scope with citable literature grounding per layer, the composition addresses field's top unsolved challenges because the mechanism being validated is explicit at each layer, and if you are building generative agents whose architecture depends on an LLM to fill in unmodeled layers the ten-layer composition is one alternative architectural shape producing auditable-testable-portable behavior at the cost of substantially more upfront engineering per layer.

### 178. When a Latent Bug Went Undetected for Twenty-Seven Days Until a Consumer Project's Pre-Commit Hook Caught It — Cross-Consumer Typecheck as Session-Close Extension

**Date:** 2026-07-06

Methodology finding: sim-ai LandmarkEvent field-name mismatch (`subjectSimId`/`type`/`valenceImpact` where schema uses `actorSimId`/`eventType`/`affectiveMagnitude`) shipped at Phase 3.2-D H-NEW-2 Q56 a7Memory tick loop integration on 2026-07-05 evening commit 05b843b silently degraded landmark memory encoding to `baseValenceImpact=0` for 27 days. Discovery pathway: unrelated post-Phase-11 loose-end sweep polish_queue Item 353 commit at Open Alley whose pre-commit hook runs `npm run typecheck` against aliased sim-ai code surfaced 8 typecheck errors including the 3 landmark field-name references. Sim-ai had NO pre-commit hook; Open Alley DID. Asymmetric bug-detection surface via cross-consumer typecheck. Sub-shape 22 architectural-extension-awareness discipline strengthens to n+3 within-Phase-3 (Post 0168 origination + Post 0174 within-session recurrence + this post 27-day-latent recurrence at a7Memory landmark-encoding surface). Prevention shipped: sim-ai `scripts/install-hooks.sh` installing `.git/hooks/pre-commit` running typecheck + `package.json` typecheck script + `landmarkValenceSign` helper mapping exposure_crisis to negative-valence + 5 additional pre-existing typecheck errors fixed. Council #9 Item 12 filed for cross-consumer-typecheck-as-latent-bug-detection-surface candidate methodology observation with 4 review questions covering promotion pathway (Session-Close 7th Stage vs Rule 20 read-side sub-shape vs remain-as-observation). Full suite 863/863 still pass.

## What's next

This repo will keep growing as new posts publish. Numbered ordering means new posts get the next number (0163 and so on) and join the bottom of the per-post summaries above; the 0107-0109 retracted-duplicate gap is preserved as visible record of the audit-caught duplication event and is not refilled. The intro at the top updates as the framework's research direction develops; new entries in the canonical record produce new posts that document specific empirical fires, discipline responses, methodological observations, product-feature lessons, methodology-canonization-direction posts, or philosophical-content-arc contributions to procedural-character architecture as they emerge.
